	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Mozart" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Mozart_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Mozart (disambiguation)">Mozart (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Austrian composer of the Classical period</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti class="thumbcaption">Anonymous portrait of the child Mozart, possibly by <a href="/wiki/Pietro_Antonio_Lorenzoni" title="Pietro Antonio Lorenzoni">Pietro Antonio Lorenzoni</a>; painted in 1763 on commission from Leopold Mozart</div></div></div></div></div>
<p><b>Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</b><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> (27 January 1756&#160;– 5 December 1791), baptised as <b>Johannes Chrysostomus Wolfgangus Theophilus Mozart</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> was a prolific and influential composer of the <a href="/wiki/Classical_period_(music)" title="Classical period (music)">classical era</a>.
</p><p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>, Mozart showed prodigious ability from his earliest childhood. Already competent on <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">keyboard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a>, he composed from the age of five and performed before European royalty. At 17, Mozart was engaged as a musician at the Salzburg court but grew restless and travelled in search of a better position. While visiting <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a> in 1781, he was dismissed from his Salzburg position. He chose to stay in the capital, where he achieved fame but little financial security. During his final years in Vienna, he composed many of his best-known <a href="/wiki/List_of_symphonies_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of symphonies by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">symphonies</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart#Concertos" title="List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">concertos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_operas_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">operas</a>, and portions of the <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a>, which was largely unfinished at the time of his early death at the age of 35. The circumstances of his death have been much mythologized.
</p><p>He composed more than 600 works, many of which are acknowledged as pinnacles of <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphonic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Concerto" title="Concerto">concertante</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chamber_music" title="Chamber music">chamber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Opera" title="Opera">operatic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choral</a> music. He is among the most enduringly popular of <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical</a> composers, and his influence is profound on subsequent Western art music. <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> composed his early works in the shadow of Mozart, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a> wrote: "posterity will not see such a talent again in 100 years".<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_career">Life and career</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/180px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/270px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg/360px-Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg 2x" data-file-width="566" data-file-height="866" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Casa_natale_di_Mozart.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart's birthplace at Getreidegasse 9, Salzburg</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_and_childhood">Family and childhood</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_name" title="Mozart&#39;s name">Mozart's name</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_family" title="Mozart family">Mozart family</a></div>
<p>Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart was born on 27<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>January 1756 to <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Mozart" title="Leopold Mozart">Leopold Mozart</a> (1719–1787) and <a href="/wiki/Anna_Maria_Mozart" title="Anna Maria Mozart">Anna Maria</a>, née Pertl (1720–1778), at <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_birthplace" title="Mozart&#39;s birthplace">9&#160;Getreidegasse</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>  This was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Salzburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Salzburg">Archbishopric of Salzburg</a>, an ecclesiastic principality in what is now <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, then part of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> He was the youngest of seven children, five of whom died in infancy. His elder sister was <a href="/wiki/Maria_Anna_Mozart" title="Maria Anna Mozart">Maria Anna Mozart</a> (1751–1829), nicknamed "Nannerl". Mozart was baptised the day after his birth, at <a href="/wiki/Salzburg_Cathedral" title="Salzburg Cathedral">St. Rupert's Cathedral</a> in Salzburg. The baptismal record gives his name in Latinized form, as <i>Joannes Chrysostomus Wolfgangus Theophilus Mozart</i>. He generally called himself "Wolfgang Amadè Mozart"<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> as an adult, but <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_name" title="Mozart&#39;s name">his name</a> had many variants.
</p><p>Leopold Mozart, a native of <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Germany, was a minor composer and an experienced teacher. In 1743, he was appointed as fourth violinist in the musical establishment of <a href="/wiki/Count_Leopold_Anton_von_Firmian" title="Count Leopold Anton von Firmian">Count Leopold Anton von Firmian</a>, the ruling <a href="/wiki/Archbishopric_of_Salzburg#Prince-Bishopric_(1213–1803)" class="mw-redirect" title="Archbishopric of Salzburg">Prince-Archbishop of Salzburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisen_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisen-8">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Four years later, he married Anna Maria in Salzburg. Leopold became the orchestra's deputy <a href="/wiki/Kapellmeister" title="Kapellmeister">Kapellmeister</a> in 1763. During the year of his son's birth, Leopold published a violin textbook, <i><a href="/wiki/Versuch_einer_gr%C3%BCndlichen_Violinschule" title="Versuch einer gründlichen Violinschule">Versuch einer gründlichen Violinschule</a></i>, which achieved success.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon199532_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon199532-9">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When Nannerl was 7, she began keyboard lessons with her father, while her three-year-old brother looked on. Years later, after her brother's death, she reminisced:
</p>
<blockquote><p>He often spent much time at the <a href="/wiki/Keyboard_instrument" title="Keyboard instrument">clavier</a>, picking out thirds, which he was ever striking, and his pleasure showed that it sounded good.... In the fourth year of his age his father, for a game as it were, began to teach him a few minuets and pieces at the clavier.... He could play it faultlessly and with the greatest delicacy, and keeping exactly in time.... At the age of five, he was already composing little pieces, which he played to his father who wrote them down.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_(Salzbourg,_1756-Vienne,_1791)_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/170px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="266" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/255px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_%28Salzbourg%2C_1756-Vienne%2C_1791%29_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/340px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3322" data-file-height="5203" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Louis_Carrogis_dit_Carmontelle_-_Portrait_de_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_(Salzbourg,_1756-Vienne,_1791)_jouant_%C3%A0_Paris_avec_son_p%C3%A8re_Jean..._-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Mozart family on tour: Leopold, Wolfgang, and Nannerl. Watercolour by <a href="/wiki/Louis_Carrogis_Carmontelle" title="Louis Carrogis Carmontelle">Carmontelle</a>, ca.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1763<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>These early pieces, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6chel_catalogue" title="Köchel catalogue">K.</a> 1–5, were recorded in the <i><a href="/wiki/Nannerl_Notenbuch" title="Nannerl Notenbuch">Nannerl Notenbuch</a></i>. There is some scholarly debate about whether Mozart was four or five years old when he created his first musical compositions, though there is little doubt that Mozart composed his first three pieces of music within a few weeks of each other: K. 1a, 1b, and 1c.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his early years, Wolfgang's father was his only teacher. Along with music, he taught his children languages and academic subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_39_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_39-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Solomon notes that, while Leopold was a devoted teacher to his children, there is evidence that Mozart was keen to progress beyond what he was taught.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_39_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_39-13">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His first ink-spattered composition and his precocious efforts with the violin were of his initiative and came as a surprise to Leopold,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> who eventually gave up composing when his son's musical talents became evident.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="1762.E2.80.9373:_Travel"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1762–73:_Travel">1762–73: Travel</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mozart_family_grand_tour" title="Mozart family grand tour">Mozart family grand tour</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_in_Italy" title="Mozart in Italy">Mozart in Italy</a></div>
<p>While Wolfgang was young, his family made several European journeys in which he and Nannerl performed as <a href="/wiki/Child_prodigy" title="Child prodigy">child prodigies</a>. These began with an exhibition in 1762 at the court of <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">Prince-elector</a> <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_III_Joseph,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian III Joseph, Elector of Bavaria">Maximilian III</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavaria</a> in Munich, and at the Imperial Courts in Vienna and Prague. A long concert tour followed, spanning three and a half years, taking the family to the courts of Munich, <a href="/wiki/Mannheim" title="Mannheim">Mannheim</a>, Paris, London,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a>, again to Paris, and back home via Zurich, <a href="/wiki/Donaueschingen" title="Donaueschingen">Donaueschingen</a>, and Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>  During this trip, Wolfgang met many musicians and acquainted himself with the works of other composers. A particularly significant influence was <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Bach" title="Johann Christian Bach">Johann Christian Bach</a>, whom he visited in London in 1764 and 1765. When he was eight years old, Mozart wrote his first symphony, most of which was probably transcribed by his father.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg/220px-MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg/330px-MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg/440px-MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="471" data-file-height="580" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MozartVeronadallaRosa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart aged 14 in January 1770</div></div></div>
<p>The family trips were often challenging, and travel conditions were primitive.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> They had to wait for invitations and reimbursement from the nobility, and they endured long, near-fatal illnesses far from home: first Leopold (London, summer 1764),<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> then both children (The Hague, autumn 1765).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The family again went to Vienna in late 1767 and remained there until December 1768.
</p><p>After one year in Salzburg, Leopold and Wolfgang set off for Italy, leaving Anna Maria and Nannerl at home. This tour lasted from December 1769 to March 1771. As with earlier journeys, Leopold wanted to display his son's abilities as a performer and a rapidly maturing composer. Wolfgang met <a href="/wiki/Josef_Myslive%C4%8Dek" title="Josef Mysliveček">Josef Mysliveček</a> and <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Martini" title="Giovanni Battista Martini">Giovanni Battista Martini</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bologna" title="Bologna">Bologna</a> and was accepted as a member of the famous <a href="/wiki/Accademia_Filarmonica_di_Bologna" title="Accademia Filarmonica di Bologna">Accademia Filarmonica</a>. In Rome, he heard <a href="/wiki/Gregorio_Allegri" title="Gregorio Allegri">Gregorio Allegri</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Miserere_(Allegri)" title="Miserere (Allegri)">Miserere</a></i> twice in performance, in the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a>, and wrote it out from memory, thus producing the first unauthorized copy of this closely guarded property of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Vatican</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Milan, Mozart wrote the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Mitridate,_re_di_Ponto" title="Mitridate, re di Ponto">Mitridate, re di Ponto</a></i> (1770), which was performed with success. This led to further opera <a href="/wiki/Commission_(art)" title="Commission (art)">commissions</a>. He returned with his father twice to Milan (August–December 1771; October 1772&#160;– March 1773) for the composition and premieres of <i><a href="/wiki/Ascanio_in_Alba" title="Ascanio in Alba">Ascanio in Alba</a></i> (1771) and <i><a href="/wiki/Lucio_Silla" title="Lucio Silla">Lucio Silla</a></i> (1772). Leopold hoped that these visits would result in a professional appointment for his son, and indeed ruling <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Karl,_Archduke_of_Austria-Este" title="Ferdinand Karl, Archduke of Austria-Este">Archduke Ferdinand</a> contemplated hiring Mozart but owing to his mother <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa" title="Maria Theresa">Empress Maria Theresa</a>'s reluctance to employ "useless people", the matter was dropped,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> and Leopold's hopes were never realized.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Toward the end of the journey, Mozart wrote the solo <a href="/wiki/Motet" title="Motet">motet</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Exsultate,_jubilate" title="Exsultate, jubilate">Exsultate, jubilate</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6chel_catalogue" title="Köchel catalogue">K.</a>&#160;165.
</p>
<h3><span id="1773.E2.80.9377:_Employment_at_the_Salzburg_court"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1773–77:_Employment_at_the_Salzburg_court">1773–77: Employment at the Salzburg court</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/170px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/255px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg/340px-Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2320" data-file-height="3536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart%27s_old_home.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzmeisterhaus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tanzmeisterhaus (page does not exist)">Tanzmeisterhaus</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanzmeisterhaus" class="extiw" title="de:Tanzmeisterhaus">de</a>&#93;</span>, Salzburg, Mozart family residence from 1773; reconstructed 1996</div></div></div>
<p>After finally returning with his father from Italy on 13 March 1773, Mozart was employed as a court musician by the ruler of Salzburg, <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_von_Colloredo_(1732%E2%80%931812)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hieronymus von Colloredo (1732–1812)">Prince-Archbishop Hieronymus Colloredo</a>. The composer had many friends and admirers in Salzburg<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and had the opportunity to work in many genres, including symphonies, sonatas, string quartets, <a href="/wiki/Mass_(music)" title="Mass (music)">masses</a>, serenades, and a few minor operas. Between April and December 1775, Mozart developed an enthusiasm for violin concertos, producing a series of five (the only ones he ever wrote), which steadily increased in their musical sophistication. The last three—<a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._3_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 3 (Mozart)">K.&#160;216</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._4_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 4 (Mozart)">K.&#160;218</a>, <a href="/wiki/Violin_Concerto_No._5_(Mozart)" title="Violin Concerto No. 5 (Mozart)">K.&#160;219</a>—are now staples of the repertoire. In 1776, he turned his efforts to <a href="/wiki/Mozart_piano_concertos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart piano concertos">piano concertos</a>, culminating in the E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span> concerto <a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._9_(Mozart)" title="Piano Concerto No. 9 (Mozart)">K.&#160;271</a> of early 1777, considered by critics to be a breakthrough work.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite these artistic successes, Mozart grew increasingly discontented with Salzburg and redoubled his efforts to find a position elsewhere. One reason was his low salary, 150 florins a year;<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Mozart longed to compose operas, and Salzburg provided only rare occasions for these. The situation worsened in 1775 when the court theatre was closed, especially since the other theatre in Salzburg was primarily reserved for visiting troupes.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two long expeditions in search of work interrupted this long Salzburg stay. Mozart and his father visited Vienna from 14 July to 26 September 1773, and Munich from 6 December 1774 to March 1775. Neither visit was successful, though the Munich journey resulted in a popular success with the premiere of Mozart's opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_finta_giardiniera" title="La finta giardiniera">La finta giardiniera</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1777.E2.80.9378:_Journey_to_Paris"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1777–78:_Journey_to_Paris">1777–78: Journey to Paris</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/170px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/255px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg/340px-Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3003" data-file-height="3460" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martini_bologna_mozart_1777.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mozart wearing the badge of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Golden_Spur" title="Order of the Golden Spur">Order of the Golden Spur</a> that he received in 1770 from <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XIV" title="Pope Clement XIV">Pope Clement XIV</a> in Rome. The painting is a 1777 copy of a work now lost.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In August 1777, Mozart resigned his position at Salzburg<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;e&#93;</a></sup> and on 23 September ventured out once more in search of employment, with visits to <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a>, Mannheim, Paris, and Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart became acquainted with members of the famous orchestra in Mannheim, the best in Europe at the time. He also fell in love with <a href="/wiki/Aloysia_Weber" title="Aloysia Weber">Aloysia Weber</a>, one of four daughters of a musical family. There were prospects of employment in Mannheim, but they came to nothing,<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and Mozart left for Paris on 14 March 1778<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> to continue his search. One of his letters from Paris hints at a possible post as an organist at <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">Versailles</a>, but Mozart was not interested in such an appointment.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He fell into debt and took to pawning valuables.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The nadir of the visit occurred when Mozart's mother was taken ill and died on 3 July 1778.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> There had been delays in calling a doctor—probably, according to Halliwell, because of a lack of funds.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Mozart stayed with <a href="/wiki/Melchior_Grimm" class="mw-redirect" title="Melchior Grimm">Melchior Grimm</a>, who, as a personal secretary of the <a href="/wiki/Louis_Philippe_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Louis Philippe I, Duke of Orléans">Duke d'Orléans</a>, lived in his mansion.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While Mozart was in Paris, his father was pursuing opportunities of employment for him in Salzburg.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> With the support of the local nobility, Mozart was offered a post as court organist and concertmaster. The annual salary was 450 florins,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> but he was reluctant to accept.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> By that time, relations between Grimm and Mozart had cooled, and Mozart moved out. After leaving Paris in September 1778 for Strasbourg, he lingered in Mannheim and Munich, still hoping to obtain an appointment outside Salzburg. In Munich, he again encountered Aloysia, now a very successful singer, but she was no longer interested in him.<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_3_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_3-45">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Mozart finally returned to Salzburg on 15 January 1779 and took up his new appointment, but his discontentment with Salzburg remained undiminished.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among the better-known works which Mozart wrote on the Paris journey are the <a href="/wiki/Piano_Sonata_No._8_(Mozart)" title="Piano Sonata No. 8 (Mozart)">A minor piano sonata</a>, K.&#160;310/300d and the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._31_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 31 (Mozart)">"Paris" Symphony</a> (No.&#160;31), which were performed in Paris on 12 and 18 June 1778.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vienna">Vienna</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_operas_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">List of operas by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1781:_Departure">1781: Departure</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/220px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/330px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg/440px-Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1520" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Croce_MozartFamilyPortrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mozart_family" title="Mozart family">Mozart family</a> c. 1780 (<a href="/wiki/Johann_Nepomuk_della_Croce" title="Johann Nepomuk della Croce">della Croce</a>); the portrait on the wall is of Mozart's mother.</div></div></div>
<p>In January 1781, Mozart's opera <i><a href="/wiki/Idomeneo" title="Idomeneo">Idomeneo</a></i> premiered with "considerable success" in Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The following March, Mozart was summoned to Vienna, where his employer, Archbishop Colloredo, was attending the celebrations for the accession of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a> to the Austrian throne. For Colloredo, this was simply a matter of wanting his musical servant to be at hand (Mozart indeed was required to dine in Colloredo's establishment with the valets and cooks.)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;f&#93;</a></sup> However, Mozart was planning a bigger career even as he continued in the archbishop's service;<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238-51">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> for example, he wrote to his father:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>My main goal right now is to meet the emperor in some agreeable fashion, I am absolutely determined he <em>should get to know me</em>. I would be so happy if I could whip through my opera for him and then play a fugue or two, for that's what he likes.<sup id="cite_ref-Spaethling237_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spaethling237-52">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Mozart did indeed soon meet the Emperor, who eventually was to support his career substantially with commissions and a part-time position.
</p><p>In the same letter to his father just quoted, Mozart outlined his plans to participate as a soloist in the concerts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Tonk%C3%BCnstler-Societ%C3%A4t" title="Tonkünstler-Societät">Tonkünstler-Societät</a></i>, a prominent benefit concert series;<sup id="cite_ref-Spaethling237_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spaethling237-52">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> this plan as well came to pass after the local nobility prevailed on Colloredo to drop his opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238–39_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESpaethling2000238–39-53">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Colloredo's wish to prevent Mozart from performing outside his establishment was in other cases, however, carried through, raising the composer's anger; one example was a chance to perform before the Emperor at <a href="/wiki/Maria_Wilhelmine_Thun" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Wilhelmine Thun">Countess Thun</a>'s for a fee equal to half of his yearly Salzburg salary.
</p><p>The quarrel with the archbishop came to a head in May: Mozart attempted to resign and was refused. The following month, permission was granted, but in a grossly insulting way: the composer was dismissed literally "with a kick in the arse", administered by the archbishop's steward, Count Arco. Mozart decided to settle in Vienna as a freelance performer and composer.<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-54">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The quarrel with the archbishop went harder for Mozart because his father sided against him. Hoping fervently that he would obediently follow Colloredo back to Salzburg, Mozart's father exchanged intense letters with his son, urging him to be reconciled with their employer. Mozart passionately defended his intention to pursue an independent career in Vienna. The debate ended when Mozart was dismissed by the archbishop, freeing himself both of his employer and his father's demands to return. Solomon characterizes Mozart's resignation as a "revolutionary step", and it significantly altered the course of his life.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Haydn_and_Mozart" title="Haydn and Mozart">Haydn and Mozart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_Freemasonry" title="Mozart and Freemasonry">Mozart and Freemasonry</a></div>
<p>Mozart's new career in Vienna began well. He often performed as a pianist, notably in a competition before the Emperor with <a href="/wiki/Muzio_Clementi" title="Muzio Clementi">Muzio Clementi</a> on 24 December 1781,<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-54">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and he soon "had established himself as the finest keyboard player in Vienna".<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-54">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> He also prospered as a composer, and in 1782 completed the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Entf%C3%BChrung_aus_dem_Serail" title="Die Entführung aus dem Serail">Die Entführung aus dem Serail</a></i> ("The Abduction from the Seraglio"), which premiered on 16 July 1782 and achieved considerable success. The work was soon being performed "throughout German-speaking Europe",<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_4_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_4-54">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> and thoroughly established Mozart's reputation as a composer.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/170px-Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="221" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/255px-Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg/340px-Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1832" data-file-height="2382" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Costanze_Mozart_by_Lange_1782.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1782 portrait of <a href="/wiki/Constanze_Mozart" title="Constanze Mozart">Constanze Mozart</a> by her brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lange" title="Joseph Lange">Joseph Lange</a></div></div></div>
<p>Near the height of his quarrels with Colloredo, Mozart moved in with the Weber family, who had moved to Vienna from Mannheim. The father, Fridolin, had died, and the Webers were now taking in lodgers to make ends meet.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_children">Marriage and children</span></h4>
<p>Aloysia, who had earlier rejected Mozart's suit, was now married to the actor and artist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lange" title="Joseph Lange">Joseph Lange</a>. Mozart's interest shifted to the third Weber daughter, <a href="/wiki/Constanze_Mozart" title="Constanze Mozart">Constanze</a>.
</p><p>The courtship did not go entirely smoothly; surviving correspondence indicates that Mozart and Constanze briefly separated in April 1782.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Mozart faced a challenging task in getting his father's permission for the marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Sol258_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sol258-58">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The couple were finally married on 4 August 1782 in <a href="/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Cathedral,_Vienna" title="St. Stephen&#39;s Cathedral, Vienna">St. Stephen's Cathedral</a>, the day before his father's consent arrived in the mail.<sup id="cite_ref-Sol258_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sol258-58">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The couple had six children, of whom only two survived infancy:
</p>
<ul><li>Raimund Leopold (17 June&#160;– 19 August 1783)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Thomas_Mozart" title="Karl Thomas Mozart">Karl Thomas Mozart</a> (21 September 1784&#160;– 31 October 1858)</li>
<li>Johann Thomas Leopold (18 October&#160;– 15 November 1786)</li>
<li>Theresia Constanzia Adelheid Friedericke Maria Anna (27 December 1787&#160;– 29 June 1788)</li>
<li>Anna Maria (died soon after birth, 16 November 1789)<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Wolfgang_Mozart" title="Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart">Franz Xaver Wolfgang Mozart</a> (26 July 1791&#160;– 29 July 1844)</li></ul>
<h3><span id="1782.E2.80.9387"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1782–87">1782–87</span></h3>
<p>In 1782 and 1783, Mozart became intimately acquainted with the work of <a href="/wiki/Johann_Sebastian_Bach" title="Johann Sebastian Bach">Johann Sebastian Bach</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_Frideric_Handel" title="George Frideric Handel">George Frideric Handel</a> as a result of the influence of <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten" title="Gottfried van Swieten">Gottfried van Swieten</a>, who owned many manuscripts of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a> masters. Mozart's study of these scores inspired compositions in Baroque style and later influenced his musical language, for example in <a href="/wiki/Fugue" title="Fugue">fugal</a> passages in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">Die Zauberflöte</a></i> ("The Magic Flute") and the finale of <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._41_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 41 (Mozart)">Symphony No.&#160;41</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisen_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisen-8">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1783, Mozart and his wife visited his family in Salzburg. His father and sister were cordially polite to Constanze, but the visit prompted the composition of one of Mozart's great liturgical pieces, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Mass_in_C_minor" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Mass in C minor">Mass in C minor</a>. Though not completed, it was premiered in Salzburg, with Constanze singing a solo part.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart met <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a> in Vienna around 1784, and the two composers became friends. When Haydn visited Vienna, they sometimes played together in an impromptu <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartet</a>. Mozart's <a href="/wiki/Haydn_Quartets_(Mozart)" title="Haydn Quartets (Mozart)">six quartets dedicated to Haydn</a> (K.&#160;387, K.&#160;421, K.&#160;428, K.&#160;458, K.&#160;464, and K.&#160;465) date from the period 1782 to 1785, and are judged to be a response to Haydn's <a href="/wiki/List_of_string_quartets_by_Joseph_Haydn#Opus_33_(1781)" title="List of string quartets by Joseph Haydn">Opus 33</a> set from 1781.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Haydn in 1785 told Mozart's father: "I tell you before God, and as an honest man, your son is the greatest composer known to me by person and repute, he has taste and what is more the greatest skill in composition."<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1782 to 1785 Mozart mounted concerts with himself as a soloist, presenting three or four new piano concertos in each season. Since space in the theatres was scarce, he booked unconventional venues: a large room in the Trattnerhof (an apartment building), and the ballroom of the Mehlgrube (a restaurant).<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_293_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_293-63">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The concerts were very popular, and the <a href="/wiki/Mozart_piano_concertos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart piano concertos">concertos he premiered at them</a> are still firm fixtures in the repertoire. Solomon writes that during this period, Mozart created "a harmonious connection between an eager composer-performer and a delighted audience, which was given the opportunity of witnessing the transformation and perfection of a major musical genre".<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_293_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_293-63">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With substantial returns from his concerts and elsewhere, Mozart and his wife adopted a rather luxurious lifestyle. They moved to an expensive apartment, with a yearly rent of 460 florins.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_298_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_298-64">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Mozart bought a fine <a href="/wiki/Fortepiano" title="Fortepiano">fortepiano</a> from <a href="/wiki/Anton_Walter" title="Anton Walter">Anton Walter</a> for about 900 florins, and a <a href="/wiki/Carom_billiards" title="Carom billiards">billiard</a> table for about 300.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_298_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_298-64">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The Mozarts sent their son <a href="/wiki/Karl_Thomas_Mozart" title="Karl Thomas Mozart">Karl Thomas</a> to an expensive boarding school<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and kept servants. Saving was therefore impossible, and the short period of financial success did nothing to soften the hardship the Mozarts were later to experience.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 December 1784, Mozart became a <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">Freemason</a>, admitted to the lodge Zur Wohltätigkeit ("Beneficence").<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Freemasonry played an essential role in the remainder of Mozart's life: he attended meetings, a number of his friends were Masons, and on various occasions, he composed Masonic music, e.g. the <a href="/wiki/Maurerische_Trauermusik" title="Maurerische Trauermusik">Maurerische Trauermusik</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="1786.E2.80.9387:_Return_to_opera"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1786–87:_Return_to_opera">1786–87: Return to opera</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/170px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/255px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg/340px-Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="2560" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart%C5%AFv_klav%C3%ADr_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fortepiano" title="Fortepiano">Fortepiano</a> played by Mozart in 1787, Czech Museum of Music, Prague<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div> 
<p>Despite the great success of <i><a href="/wiki/Die_Entf%C3%BChrung_aus_dem_Serail" title="Die Entführung aus dem Serail">Die Entführung aus dem Serail</a></i>, Mozart did little operatic writing for the next four years, producing only two unfinished works and the one-act <i><a href="/wiki/Der_Schauspieldirektor" title="Der Schauspieldirektor">Der Schauspieldirektor</a></i>. He focused instead on his career as a piano soloist and writer of concertos. Around the end of 1785, Mozart moved away from keyboard writing<sup id="cite_ref-harvnb&#124;Solomon&#124;1995_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvnb|Solomon|1995-72">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (September 2010)">page&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and began his famous operatic collaboration with the <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">librettist</a> <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Da_Ponte" title="Lorenzo Da Ponte">Lorenzo Da Ponte</a>. 1786 saw the successful premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marriage_of_Figaro" title="The Marriage of Figaro">The Marriage of Figaro</a></i> in Vienna. Its reception in <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_Prague" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart and Prague">Prague</a> later in the year was even warmer, and this led to a second collaboration with Da Ponte: the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a></i>, which premiered in October 1787 to acclaim in Prague, but less success in Vienna in 1788.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  The two are among Mozart's most famous works and are mainstays of the operatic repertoire today, though at their premieres their musical complexity caused difficulty for both listeners and performers. These developments were not witnessed by Mozart's father, who had died on 28 May 1787.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 1787, Mozart finally obtained a steady post under aristocratic patronage. Emperor Joseph II appointed him as his "chamber composer", a post that had fallen vacant the previous month on the death of <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Willibald_Gluck" title="Christoph Willibald Gluck">Gluck</a>. It was a part-time appointment, paying just 800 florins per year, and required Mozart only to compose dances for the annual balls in the <a href="/wiki/Hofburg_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Hofburg Palace">Redoutensaal</a> (see <i><a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_dance" title="Mozart and dance">Mozart and dance</a></i>).  This modest income became important to Mozart when hard times arrived. Court records show that Joseph aimed to keep the esteemed composer from leaving Vienna in pursuit of better prospects.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_423_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_423-75">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;g&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1787, the young <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Ludwig van Beethoven</a> spent several weeks in Vienna, hoping to study with Mozart.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> No reliable records survive to indicate <a href="/wiki/Beethoven_and_Mozart" title="Beethoven and Mozart">whether the two composers ever met</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_years">Later years</span></h3>
<h4><span id="1788.E2.80.9390"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1788–90">1788–90</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_Berlin_journey" title="Mozart&#39;s Berlin journey">Mozart's Berlin journey</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/170px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="190" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/255px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg/340px-Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg 2x" data-file-width="499" data-file-height="558" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_drawing_Doris_Stock_1789.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Drawing of Mozart in <a href="/wiki/Silverpoint" title="Silverpoint">silverpoint</a>, made by <a href="/wiki/Dora_Stock" title="Dora Stock">Dora Stock</a> during Mozart's visit to Dresden, April 1789</div></div></div>
<p>Toward the end of the decade, Mozart's circumstances worsened. Around 1786 he had ceased to appear frequently in public concerts, and his income shrank.<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_6_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_6-78">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> This was a difficult time for musicians in Vienna because of the <a href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_(1787%E2%80%931791)" class="mw-redirect" title="Austro-Turkish War (1787–1791)">Austro-Turkish War</a>:  both the general level of prosperity and the ability of the aristocracy to support music had declined.<sup id="cite_ref-harvnb&#124;Solomon&#124;1995_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-harvnb|Solomon|1995-72">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By mid-1788, Mozart and his family had moved from central Vienna to the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Alsergrund" title="Alsergrund">Alsergrund</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sadie_1998_6_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sadie_1998_6-78">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Although it has been suggested that Mozart aimed to reduce his rental expenses, research shows that by moving to the suburb, Mozart had not reduced his expenses (as he wrote in his letter to <a href="/wiki/Michael_von_Puchberg" title="Michael von Puchberg">Puchberg</a>), but merely increased the housing space at his disposal.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Mozart began to borrow money, most often from his friend and fellow Mason <a href="/wiki/Michael_von_Puchberg" title="Michael von Puchberg">Michael Puchberg</a>; "a pitiful sequence of letters pleading for loans" survives.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Maynard Solomon and others have suggested that Mozart was suffering from depression, and it seems that his output slowed.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Major works of the period include the last three symphonies (Nos.&#160;<a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._39_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 39 (Mozart)">39</a>, <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._40_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 40 (Mozart)">40</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._41_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 41 (Mozart)">41</a>, all from 1788), and the last of the three Da Ponte operas, <i><a href="/wiki/Cos%C3%AC_fan_tutte" title="Così fan tutte">Così fan tutte</a></i>, premiered in 1790.
</p><p>Around this time, Mozart made some long journeys hoping to improve his fortunes: to <a href="/wiki/Leipzig" title="Leipzig">Leipzig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>, and Berlin in the spring of 1789, and <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a>, Mannheim, and other German cities in 1790.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1791">1791</span></h4>
<p>Mozart's last year was, until his final illness struck, a time of high productivity—and by some accounts, one of personal recovery.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;h&#93;</a></sup> He composed a great deal, including some of his most admired works: the opera <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">The Magic Flute</a></i>; the final piano concerto (<a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._27_(Mozart)" title="Piano Concerto No. 27 (Mozart)">K.&#160;595 in B<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span></a>); the <a href="/wiki/Clarinet_Concerto_(Mozart)" title="Clarinet Concerto (Mozart)">Clarinet Concerto</a> K.&#160;622; the last in his series of string quintets (<a href="/wiki/String_Quintet_No._6_(Mozart)" title="String Quintet No. 6 (Mozart)">K.&#160;614 in E<span class="music-symbol" style="font-family: Arial Unicode MS, Lucida Sans Unicode;"><span class="music-flat">&#x266d;</span></span></a>); the motet <a href="/wiki/Ave_verum_corpus_(Mozart)" title="Ave verum corpus (Mozart)">Ave verum corpus</a> K.&#160;618; and the unfinished <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a> K.&#160;626.
</p><p>Mozart's financial situation, a source of anxiety in 1790, finally began to improve. Although the evidence is inconclusive,<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-84">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> it appears that wealthy patrons in Hungary and Amsterdam pledged annuities to Mozart in return for the occasional composition. He is thought to have benefited from the sale of dance music written in his role as Imperial chamber composer.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-84">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Mozart no longer borrowed large sums from Puchberg and made a start on paying off his debts.<sup id="cite_ref-solomon_1995_477_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-solomon_1995_477-84">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He experienced great satisfaction in the public success of some of his works, notably <i>The Magic Flute</i> (which was performed several times in the short period between its premiere and Mozart's death)<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and the Little Masonic Cantata K.&#160;623, premiered on 17 November 1791.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_illness_and_death">Final illness and death</span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Death of Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a></div>
<p>Mozart fell ill while in Prague for the 6 September 1791 premiere of his opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_clemenza_di_Tito" title="La clemenza di Tito">La clemenza di Tito</a></i>, written in that same year on commission for the Emperor's coronation festivities.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> He continued his professional functions for some time and conducted the premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Magic_Flute" title="The Magic Flute">The Magic Flute</a></i> on 30 September. His health deteriorated on 20&#160;November, at which point he became bedridden, suffering from swelling, pain, and vomiting.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995491_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995491-88">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/170px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/255px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg/340px-Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1392" data-file-height="1784" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang-amadeus-mozart_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Posthumous painting by <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Krafft" title="Barbara Krafft">Barbara Krafft</a> in 1819</div></div></div>
<p>Mozart was nursed in his final illness by his wife and her youngest sister and was attended by the family doctor, Thomas Franz Closset. He was mentally occupied with the task of finishing his <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem</a>, but the evidence that he dictated passages to his student <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_S%C3%BCssmayr" title="Franz Xaver Süssmayr">Franz Xaver Süssmayr</a> is minimal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESolomon1995493,_588_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESolomon1995493,_588-89">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart died in his home on 5 December 1791<span style="display:none">(1791-12-05)</span> (aged&#160;35) at 12:55 am.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/The_Grove_Dictionary_of_Music_and_Musicians" class="mw-redirect" title="The Grove Dictionary of Music and Musicians">New Grove</a></i> describes his funeral:
</p>
<blockquote><p>Mozart was interred in a common grave, in accordance with contemporary Viennese custom, at the <a href="/wiki/St._Marx_Cemetery" title="St. Marx Cemetery">St. Marx Cemetery</a> outside the city on 7 December. If, as later reports say, no mourners attended, that too is consistent with Viennese burial customs at the time; later <a href="/wiki/Otto_Jahn" title="Otto Jahn">Otto Jahn</a> (1856) wrote that <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Salieri" title="Antonio Salieri">Salieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_S%C3%BCssmayr" title="Franz Xaver Süssmayr">Süssmayr</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gottfried_van_Swieten" title="Gottfried van Swieten">van Swieten</a> and two other musicians were present. The tale of a storm and snow is false; the day was calm and mild.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>The expression "common grave" refers to neither a communal grave nor a pauper's grave, but an individual grave for a member of the common people (i.e., not the aristocracy).  Common graves were subject to excavation after ten years; the graves of aristocrats were not.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The cause of Mozart's death cannot be known with certainty. The official record has it as <i>hitziges Frieselfieber</i> ("severe miliary fever," referring to a rash that looks like <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet seeds</a>), more a description of the symptoms than a diagnosis. Researchers have suggested over 100 causes of death, including acute <a href="/wiki/Rheumatic_fever" title="Rheumatic fever">rheumatic fever</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Wakin_2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wakin_2010-93">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Streptococcus" title="Streptococcus">streptococcal</a> <a href="/wiki/Infection" title="Infection">infection</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Trichinosis" title="Trichinosis">trichinosis</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">influenza</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercury_poisoning" title="Mercury poisoning">mercury poisoning</a>, and a rare <a href="/wiki/Nephrology" title="Nephrology">kidney</a> ailment.<sup id="cite_ref-Wakin_2010_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wakin_2010-93">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart's modest funeral did not reflect his standing with the public as a composer; memorial services and concerts in Vienna and Prague were well-attended. Indeed, in the period immediately after his death, his reputation rose substantially. Solomon describes an "unprecedented wave of enthusiasm"<sup id="cite_ref-Solomonp499_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solomonp499-99">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> for his work; <a href="/wiki/Biographies_of_Mozart" title="Biographies of Mozart">biographies were written</a> (first by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schlichtegroll" title="Friedrich Schlichtegroll">Schlichtegroll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Niemetschek" title="Franz Xaver Niemetschek">Niemetschek</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georg_Nikolaus_von_Nissen" title="Georg Nikolaus von Nissen">Nissen</a>); and publishers vied to produce complete editions of his works.<sup id="cite_ref-Solomonp499_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Solomonp499-99">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_and_character">Appearance and character</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_(unfinished)_by_Lange_1782.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/220px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/330px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg/440px-Mozart_%28unfinished%29_by_Lange_1782.jpg 2x" data-file-width="567" data-file-height="550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_(unfinished)_by_Lange_1782.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail of portrait of Mozart by his brother-in-law Joseph Lange; for discussion of the portrait, see <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Lange" title="Joseph Lange">Joseph Lange</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mozart's physical appearance was described by tenor <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kelly_(tenor)" title="Michael Kelly (tenor)">Michael Kelly</a>, in his <i>Reminiscences</i>: "a remarkably small man, very thin and pale, with a profusion of fine, fair hair of which he was rather vain". His early biographer Niemetschek wrote, "there was nothing special about [his] physique. [...] He was small and his countenance, except for his large intense eyes, gave no signs of his genius." His facial complexion was pitted, a reminder of his <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_smallpox" title="Mozart and smallpox">childhood case of smallpox</a>. He loved elegant clothing. Kelly remembered him at a rehearsal: <span class="nowrap">"[He]</span> was on the stage with his crimson <a href="/wiki/Pelisse" title="Pelisse">pelisse</a> and gold-laced <a href="/wiki/Bicorne" title="Bicorne">cocked hat</a>, giving the time of the music to the orchestra." Based on pictures that researchers were able to find of Mozart, he seemed to wear a white wig for most of his formal occasions – researchers of the <a href="/wiki/Salzburg_Mozarteum" class="mw-redirect" title="Salzburg Mozarteum">Salzburg Mozarteum</a> declared that only 1 of his 14 portraits they had found showed him without his wig.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Of his voice, his wife later wrote that it "was a tenor, rather soft in speaking and delicate in singing, but when anything excited him, or it became necessary to exert it, it was both powerful and energetic".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart usually worked long and hard, finishing compositions at a tremendous pace as deadlines approached. He often made sketches and drafts; unlike Beethoven's, these are mostly not preserved, as his wife sought to destroy them after his death.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Mozart lived at the center of the Viennese musical world, and knew a significant number and variety of people: fellow musicians, theatrical performers, fellow Salzburgers, and aristocrats, including some acquaintance with Emperor <a href="/wiki/Joseph_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Joseph II, Holy Roman Emperor">Joseph II</a>. Solomon considers his three closest friends to have been Gottfried von Jacquin, Count August Hatzfeld, and Sigmund Barisani; others included his older colleague <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Joseph Haydn</a>, singers <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Gerl" title="Franz Xaver Gerl">Franz Xaver Gerl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benedikt_Schack" title="Benedikt Schack">Benedikt Schack</a>, and the horn player <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Leutgeb" title="Joseph Leutgeb">Joseph Leutgeb</a>. Leutgeb and Mozart carried on a curious kind of friendly mockery, often with Leutgeb as the butt of Mozart's <a href="/wiki/Practical_joke" title="Practical joke">practical jokes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He enjoyed <a href="/wiki/Billiards" class="mw-redirect" title="Billiards">billiards</a> and dancing and kept pets: a canary, a <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_starling" title="Mozart&#39;s starling">starling</a>, a dog, and a horse for recreational riding.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> He had a startling fondness for <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_scatology" title="Mozart and scatology">scatological humour</a>, which is preserved in his surviving letters, notably those written to his cousin <a href="/wiki/Maria_Anna_Thekla_Mozart" title="Maria Anna Thekla Mozart">Maria Anna Thekla Mozart</a> around 1777–1778, and in his correspondence with his sister and parents.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Mozart also wrote scatological music, a series of <a href="/wiki/Canon_(music)" title="Canon (music)">canons</a> that he sang with his friends.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mozart_and_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart and Catholicism">Mozart and Catholicism</a></div>
<p>Mozart was raised a <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> and remained a devout member of the church throughout his life.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Works.2C_musical_style.2C_and_innovations"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Works,_musical_style,_and_innovations">Works, musical style, and innovations</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_compositions_by_Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">List of compositions by Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mozart%27s_compositional_method" title="Mozart&#39;s compositional method">Mozart's compositional method</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Style">Style</span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-audio-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Symphony_40_g-moll_-_1._Molto_allegro.ogg" title="File:Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart - Symphony 40 g-moll - 1. Molto allegro.ogg">Symphonie Nr. 40 g-moll, K. 550. Movement: 1. Molto allegro</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="493.2" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Symphony_40_g-moll_-_1._Molto_allegro.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Symphony_40_g-moll_-_1._Molto_allegro.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (177 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="176740" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/99/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Symphony_40_g-moll_-_1._Molto_allegro.ogg/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Symphony_40_g-moll_-_1._Molto_allegro.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="200640" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"></div></div><hr /><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Don_Giovanni_-_Overt%C3%BCre.ogg" title="File:Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart - Don Giovanni - Overtüre.ogg">Overture to <i>Don Giovanni</i></a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="408.76" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Don_Giovanni_-_Overtüre.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Don_Giovanni_-_Overt%C3%BCre.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (196 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="196127" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/0/0a/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Don_Giovanni_-_Overt%C3%BCre.ogg/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart_-_Don_Giovanni_-_Overt%C3%BCre.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="209944" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">Both performed by the Fulda Symphonic Orchestra, Conductor: Simon Schindler</div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>Mozart's music, like <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Haydn" title="Joseph Haydn">Haydn</a>'s, stands as an archetype of the <a href="/wiki/Classical_period_(music)" title="Classical period (music)">Classical style</a>. At the time he began composing, European music was dominated by the <i><a href="/wiki/Galant" class="mw-redirect" title="Galant">style galant</a></i>, a reaction against the highly evolved intricacy of the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_music" title="Baroque music">Baroque</a>. Progressively, and in large part at the hands of Mozart himself, the <a href="/wiki/Counterpoint" title="Counterpoint">contrapuntal</a> complexities of the late Baroque emerged once more, moderated and disciplined by new <a href="/wiki/Musical_form" title="Musical form">forms</a>, and adapted to a new aesthetic and social milieu. Mozart was a versatile composer, and wrote in every major genre, including <a href="/wiki/Symphony" title="Symphony">symphony</a>, opera, the solo concerto, chamber music including <a href="/wiki/String_quartet" title="String quartet">string quartet</a> and <a href="/wiki/String_quintet" title="String quintet">string quintet</a>, and the piano <a href="/wiki/Sonata" title="Sonata">sonata</a>. These forms were not new, but Mozart advanced their technical sophistication and emotional reach. He almost single-handedly developed and popularized the Classical <a href="/wiki/Mozart_piano_concertos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart piano concertos">piano concerto</a>. He wrote a great deal of <a href="/wiki/Religious_music" title="Religious music">religious music</a>, including large-scale <a href="/wiki/Mass_(music)" title="Mass (music)">masses</a>, as well as dances, <a href="/wiki/Divertimento" title="Divertimento">divertimenti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serenade" title="Serenade">serenades</a>, and other forms of light entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The central traits of the Classical style are all present in Mozart's music. Clarity, balance, and transparency are the hallmarks of his work, but simplistic notions of its delicacy mask the exceptional power of his finest masterpieces, such as the <a href="/wiki/Piano_Concerto_No._24_(Mozart)" title="Piano Concerto No. 24 (Mozart)">Piano Concerto No. 24</a> in C minor, K.&#160;491; the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._40_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 40 (Mozart)">Symphony No.&#160;40</a> in G minor, K.&#160;550; and the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a></i>. <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rosen" title="Charles Rosen">Charles Rosen</a> makes the point forcefully:
</p>
<blockquote><p>It is only through recognizing the violence and sensuality at the center of Mozart's work that we can make a start towards a comprehension of his structures and an insight into his magnificence. In a paradoxical way, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Schumann" title="Robert Schumann">Schumann</a>'s superficial characterization of the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._40_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 40 (Mozart)">G minor Symphony</a> can help us to see Mozart's daemon more steadily. In all of Mozart's supreme expressions of suffering and terror, there is something shockingly voluptuous.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>During his last decade, Mozart frequently exploited <a href="/wiki/Chromaticism" title="Chromaticism">chromatic</a> harmony. A notable instance is his <a href="/wiki/String_Quartet_No._19_(Mozart)" title="String Quartet No. 19 (Mozart)"><i>String Quartet in C major</i>, K.&#160;465</a> (1785), whose introduction abounds in chromatic suspensions, giving rise to the work's nickname, the "Dissonance" quartet.
</p><p>Mozart always had a gift for absorbing and adapting the valuable features of others' music. His travels helped in the forging of a unique compositional language.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> In London as a child, he met <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christian_Bach" title="Johann Christian Bach">J.&#160;C. Bach</a> and heard his music. In Paris, Mannheim, and Vienna he met with other compositional influences, as well as the avant-garde capabilities of the <a href="/wiki/Mannheim_school" title="Mannheim school">Mannheim orchestra</a>. In Italy, he encountered the <a href="/wiki/Italian_overture" title="Italian overture">Italian overture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Opera_buffa" title="Opera buffa">opera buffa</a>, both of which deeply affected the evolution of his practice. In London and Italy, the galant style was in the ascendent: simple, light music with a mania for <a href="/wiki/Cadence_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadence (music)">cadencing</a>; an emphasis on tonic, dominant, and subdominant to the exclusion of other harmonies; symmetrical phrases; and clearly articulated partitions in the overall form of movements.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Some of Mozart's early symphonies are <a href="/wiki/Italian_overture" title="Italian overture">Italian overtures</a>, with three movements running into each other; many are <a href="/wiki/Homotonal" title="Homotonal">homotonal</a> (all three movements having the same key signature, with the slow middle movement being in the <a href="/wiki/Relative_key" title="Relative key">relative minor</a>). Others mimic the works of J.&#160;C. Bach, and others show the simple <a href="/wiki/Binary_form" title="Binary form">rounded binary forms</a> turned out by Viennese composers.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg/220px-Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg/330px-Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg/440px-Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mozart_Sheet_Music.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Facsimile sheet of music from the Dies Irae movement of the <a href="/wiki/Requiem_(Mozart)" title="Requiem (Mozart)">Requiem Mass in D minor</a> (K.&#160;626) in Mozart's handwriting (<a href="/wiki/Mozarthaus_Vienna" title="Mozarthaus Vienna">Mozarthaus</a>, Vienna)</div></div></div>
<p>As Mozart matured, he progressively incorporated more features adapted from the Baroque. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._29_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 29 (Mozart)">Symphony No.&#160;29 in A major</a> K.&#160;201 has a contrapuntal main theme in its first movement, and experimentation with irregular phrase lengths. Some of his quartets from 1773 have fugal finales, probably influenced by Haydn, who had included three such finales in his recently published Opus&#160;20 set. The influence of the <i><a href="/wiki/Sturm_und_Drang" title="Sturm und Drang">Sturm und Drang</a></i> ("Storm and Stress") period in music, with its brief foreshadowing of the <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic era</a>, is evident in the music of both composers at that time. Mozart's <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._25_(Mozart)" title="Symphony No. 25 (Mozart)">Symphony No.&#160;25 in G minor</a> K.&#160;183 is another excellent example.
</p><p>Mozart would sometimes switch his focus between operas and instrumental music.
